<div id="review_405268833" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/405268833" />
    <a title="Arminion" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10664177-arminion"><img alt="Arminion" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341340920p2/10664177.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/405268833?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arminion" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arminion" href="/user/show/10664177-arminion">Arminion</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781857234039" href="/book/show/568473.A_Crown_of_Swords">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer405268833&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer405268833" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12866984020986960787">A tear fell down my cheek. It was both a tear of happiness and one of sadness. I was happy that finally, after months of torture, I have finished reading Crown of Swords. But at the same time, I was sad for all the trees that were cut down to make printing of this book possible.<br/>After book 4, I started noticing certain things about Jordan prose (if you can even call it that). Here, these things were so obvious and so over the top, that they burned my eyes and consumed my soul every time I saw the</span>
  <span id="freeText12866984020986960787" style="display:none">A tear fell down my cheek. It was both a tear of happiness and one of sadness. I was happy that finally, after months of torture, I have finished reading Crown of Swords. But at the same time, I was sad for all the trees that were cut down to make printing of this book possible.<br />After book 4, I started noticing certain things about Jordan prose (if you can even call it that). Here, these things were so obvious and so over the top, that they burned my eyes and consumed my soul every time I saw them. So, here is the list:<br /><br />1) He is extremely wordy. A normal sentence, in any other decent book, would go something like this:<br /><br />"We will meet again" said Egwene. <br /><br />In Jordan's book? That same sentence goes like this: <br /><br />"We will meet again, Aviendha" said Egwene adjusting her shawl and glaring at the plump innkeeper scrubbing the floor. <br /><br />My example was actually short! Still don't believe me? Ok, then here is a sentence from chapter 28: <br /><br /><i>The third woman, tall and dark in neat gray wool, maybe a Tairen, crossed two bridges before entering a large shop where she was greeted with smiles by a skinny bowing fellow and began supervising the loading of lacquered boxes and trays into sawdust-filled baskets that were then loaded into a wagon.</i> <br /><br />Jesus, that was a mouthful. Or how about this one, in chapter 37:<br /><br /><i>Her notion of what to wear visiting the roughest part of the city without attracting attention was a wide green hat with green-dyed plumes, a light dustcloak of green linen worked in golden scrolls hanging down her back, and a high-necked green silk riding dress with gold embroidery climbing the divided skirts and thickly emphasizing the oval that exposed half her bosom.</i><br /><br />These are prime examples of sentences that are completely useless and the one that don't advance the plot. Now imagine every other sentence like that. This makes for a slow and frustrating read. This leads me to my next point:<br /><br />2) His books don't have a plot anymore. I mean they have, but it's completely meaningless and it can be summarized on one page. That should be clear just by looking at some of the names of the chapters in this book. I mean, when you have chapters like "A Bath" and "Bread and Cheese" you know there is some action packed adventure right there!<br /><br />3) I hate all the women in his books. All of them. There is not a single woman who I actually like, and care about. Well, maybe Moiraine. And maaaaybe Egwene, but that's already pushing it. They can all be described by one word. Arrogant. They are all petty, angry, irritated and pissed off. They are constantly arguing, bickering, glaring, frowning, sniffing, blushing and barking out orders. And it's always men's fault. I don't remember if I ever, in all seven books, read a chapter where women actually laughed, and they were happy, nice, polite and charming. No, there is constantly a tension and a struggle between them. Don't believe me? In chapter 31, Lan saves Nynaeve from drowning and how does she thanks him? She slaps him five times on the face and punches him in the stomach. And no, I'm not kidding. I would really wish that Jordan just kills all these women, but knowing Jordan, he would probably resurrect them after a different name. And this takes me to my next point:<br /><br />4) The characters DON'T die. They just don't. Even those that he kills come back somehow. This removes the entire tension and sense of danger out of the book. Why should I fear for Perrin's safety or Random Aes Sedai #216 when I know they won't die? Unlike the previous books, here a few people actually die. But that's a drop in the ocean. There are still 997 more characters alive.<br /><br />5) Each character has a unique name. God, this pisses me off to no end. I would understand this notion if the story had like 50 characters, or hell even 100. But Wheel of Time by this point has over 1000 characters! I know that having two different characters with same name would just further complicate things, but at least it would be realistic! I don't think anyone would be confused if there is a random innkeeper in Ebou Dar whose name is Mat. What's even worse 90% of all these characters are completely meaningless to the story! Or are they? Sometimes Jordan pulls some minor character from previous books and places him in the new one. At first I found this cool, but now it's just annoying and it gives you a sense that Randland is actually a pretty small place. I also hate how some characters have "fantasy" names like Lan, Nynaeve, Mogheiden and so on, while others have "realistic" names like Elayne and Nicole. Ugh!<br /><br />6) The Last Battle is approaching (apparently) and yet everybody thinks about some pointless things, like what dress to buy or if they should marry someone or not. Who cares, people? The end of the world, the frickin armageddon is approaching and nobody doesn't even care! Maybe Last Battle isn't the end of the world, but then what is it? It's book seven and Jordan still didn't explain it. Also, Rand is pretty much a ticking time bomb yet three girls are fighting over him. Don't they realize that he will (probably) die and kill half the humanity? Apparently not. They just want to "share" him. Ugh, I want to throw up every time I read about this. There is also a lot of other questions bubbling in my mind, like do Aes Sedai and their Warders ever sleep with each other? What am I saying? Of course not. Nobody in this series gets laid. Actually no, scratch that. We finally have a first rape scene in this book. And I say finally not because I love reading about it (quite the contrary actually), but because for some strange reason, fantasy book just can't go without at least one rape scene. But guess what. The rape victim isn't a woman. Oh no, no, it's a man! Why am I not surprised?<br /><br />7) And finally, my last point: repetition. Jordan uses two types of repetition in his books: major and minor. Major repetitions is when he describes things, cities and people that we already know how they look. Why do I have to read about Tar Valon's white towers in book seven when I did that in the previous six ones? Minor repetition are various words or actions that Jordan likes to use, again and again. I actually keep track of certain words to see how often do they appear. It makes reading more bearable, as I have my own little Easter egg hunt. Here is the list (you may check my other WoT reviews for more data if you are interested):<br /><br />Frown – 146<br />Sniff – 36<br />Braid – 46<br />Dress – 138<br />Muttering – 99<br />Silk – 110<br />Blushing – 70<br /><br />Although, I should probably add more words to that list, like: sitting cross-legged, gave a start, mouth tightening, folding arms beneath breasts, big dark eyes, ageless face, wetlander, wool, Sea Folk porcelain, skirt smoothing, shawl adjusting, licking/wetting the lips, dice spinning in Mat's head, ear-boxing, eyes bulging, and so on and so on.<br />Often times, while reading this book, I asked myself: Why is this important? The answer? It isn't.<br />I will never read another WoT book, not even for money. This is just slow, painful and meaningless drivel. This book ends my Wheel of Time adventure thank God.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12866984020986960787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8691453659199626301" style="display:none"><i>Master of the lightnings, rider on the storm,<br />wearer of a crown of swords, spinner-out of fate.<br />Who thinks he turns the Wheel of Time,<br />may learn the truth too late...</i><br /><br />It's really really hard to summarize a book like this due to its length and how far along it is in the series. Loyalties tested. Friendships called into question. Love that was once lost is now found. <br /><br />All the things that make this series fantastic continue on in this book.<br /><br />My favorite aspects of this book are that Lan and Nynaeve have finally reunited, and Cadsuane finally appears. I love that badass Aes Sedai!<br /><br />If you love long, well crafted, wonderfully characterized fantasy stories, I strongly urge you to read this series!</span>

<div id="review_927611508" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/927611508" />
    <a title="Matt Brady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7881793-matt-brady"><img alt="Matt Brady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404212164p2/7881793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/927611508?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt Brady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt Brady" href="/user/show/7881793-matt-brady">Matt Brady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8153987-a-crown-of-swords">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7881793-matt-brady?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7881793-matt-brady?shelf=wheel-of-time-reread">wheel-of-time-reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer927611508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7511538969630542420">This is a reread of the entire <i>Wheel of Time</i> so there’ll be spoilers for the whole series, both books before this and maybe books after it, ahead.<br/><br/>So I needed a bit of a break after <i>Lord of Chaos</i> turned out to be more disappointing and boring than I had remembered. I'm not the kind of guy who can tear through a big series, reading each book back to back, anyway - I get antsy if I read two books by the same author back to back, even - and that is doubly true for something as massive and, particula</span>
  <span id="freeText7511538969630542420" style="display:none">This is a reread of the entire <i>Wheel of Time</i> so there’ll be spoilers for the whole series, both books before this and maybe books after it, ahead.<br /><br />So I needed a bit of a break after <i>Lord of Chaos</i> turned out to be more disappointing and boring than I had remembered. I'm not the kind of guy who can tear through a big series, reading each book back to back, anyway - I get antsy if I read two books by the same author back to back, even - and that is doubly true for something as massive and, particular, I guess is the word, in it's style as the <i>Wheel of Time</i>. But for some reason I'm determined to finish this, especially as this whole thing started with me remembering I hadn't read the final book in the series and deciding it might be kinda cool to check it out. Fortunately <i>Crown of Swords</i> turned out to be just as disappointing and boring as I remembered!<br /><br />I'm not really going to slam <i>Crown of Swords</i> or anything. In my memory it was always just one in a long run of books in this series where nothing much happens and characters are thrown into seemingly endless subplots that arent very entertaining and seem like they're designed just to give people things to do until the final act (Perrin being sent to grab Masema, I'm looking in your direction) It has some pretty big flaws for sure - the atrocious Tylin-Mat "relationship", which has probably been talked to death and doesn't need to be covered again except to say it was very very poorly judged, the sudden introduction of Cadsuane, the most wonderful Aes Sedai who ever lived though she was literally never mentioned once before this book and who turns out to be largely exactly the same as every other Aes Sedai (except better!!!) - and not a whole lot happens until the very end of the book, which is the exact same problem <i>Lord of Chaos</i> had. But the reason I'm not being overly critical is that I realised something fairly early on in <i>Crown of Swords</i>.<br /><br />Robert Jordan cant help himself.<br /><br />Ive talked before about how it seems like every character in <i>Wheel of Time</i> seems to have a mild form of OCD, a collection of obsessive twitches and behaviours (tugging hair, sniffing, lots and lots of fingering various inanimate objects), but right from the start of <i>Crown of Swords</i> I wondered if Jordan himself didn't have some kind of writer's OCD. He begins with what seems like the best of intentions. We pick up in the immediate aftermath of Dumai Wells, one of the high points of the series, and Jordan is clearly intent on recapping what has happened and bringing readers up to speed. By the way, this is something I admire about <i>Wheel of time</i>, how well Jordan manages to recap what has happened before. It might seem silly - who's going to jump into a series with the eighth book - but as Ive mentioned before, I first started this series with <i>Fires of Heaven</i> way back when and wasn't lost at all. It's something even the best writers might not be able to say. You definitely couldn't pick up George R R Martin's <i>Feast For Crows</i> and get much of an idea of what happened in the first three books of that series, for example. In a reread it may become a bit frustrating and repetitive, but I really do admire the way Jordan tries to keep this massive sprawling series "new reader friendly". So, there he is, starting a bit of a recap. And then it starts to happen. Gradually, the chapter starts to spiral out of control. Because how can you explain Dumai Wells and it's aftermath without describing the various groups, subgroups, plots, counterplots, races, Ajahs, societies, organisations, weapons, fashion accessories, horse names. And dont forget the complicated relationships that now exist between not only every character, but various different groups of characters. Within a dozen pages, the first chapter is totally mired in minutae, and literally all that's happened is Perrin is standing around looking at people. It's that infamous <i>Wheel of Time</i> bloat, and I'm going to advance an opinion here that it's not really intentional on Jordan's part. I honestly don't think he's deliberately stalling, or dragging things out. He just genuinely cant seem to help himself. He tries to push the story along, but once he starts writing, he gets buried under the sheer weight of his own details, the burden of his own obsessive "everything and the kitchen sink" style. You can see it in the macro, but it's there in the micro too. Take Rand for example. This is a character with dragon tattoos on each arm, two heron branded palms, a never-healed painful wound in his side, a long dead madman in his head, a mental bond with an Aes Sedai, a mystical connection to Mat and Perrin, an obsessive and long list of the name of every woman that has died for, or because, of him, three women he's in love with, and, freshly added in <i>Lord of Chaos</i> a very understandable rampant claustrophobia. Once you start to "get into" Rand's head, once you try to convey to the reader what he's thinking and feeling, all these things come flooding forth, and what might have been a fairly simple and straight forward scene is now incredibly complicated by the sheer amount of weird shit that has happened to this one guy. Now expand that onto every character, every group of characters, every organisation, society, nation, etc, and you have this spreading morass that quickly bogs down every single element of the story. And that's the real problem I had with <i>Crown of Swords</i>. It's a book where Jordan finally, maybe inevitably, falls victim to his own style and has no choice but to forge ahead ever so slowly, one pointed sniff and hilt-fingering at a time.<br /><br />It ends with a decent fight against Sammael. The confrontation with Sammael isn't really built up too, but the Forsaken takedowns never are really (Belal in <i>The Dragon Reborn</i> is a total afterthought, and the big fight with Rahvin in <i>Fires of Heaven</i> feels obligatory at best, tacked on after the more satisfying climax of defeating the Shaido) The fight has some weight at least, as it's been a subplot bubbling away since early in <i>Lord of Chaos</i> at least, but it really is largely ignored for the vast majority of the book as Rand dicks around in Cairhien and Mat, Elayne and Nynaeve dick around in Ebou Dar (more minor subplots move a little more swiftly here, as Eamon Valda launches his coup of the Whitecloaks, the Seanchan invade Amadicia, but others take detours from their detour, such as the Shaido being scattered across half the world because reasons? and a hunt for the Black Ajah being launched in the Tower because Aes Sedai are just as guilty of everyone else in randland of completely misunderstanding orders) Throw in the fact that blatant sexual assault is played for humour because the victim is male, a total absence of Moiraine (still my favourite character even though she's been "dead" for two books now), very little Egwene (maybe my second favourite character) and you have a book that uhhh sure is a book. Rapey stuff aside it isn't really bad enough to trash talk, but it's never particularly good either. Unless you're a big fan of Cadsuane constantly threatening to spank a grown man, I guess?<br /><br />Next up - the next book! I'm not even exaggerating when I say I literally can't even remember what it's called!! Only four more books to go until I reach the final book which is actually split into three books!!! What am I doing with my life!!!!!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7511538969630542420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1549197565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16171360289451236736"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464420679i/19236518.jpg' width='350' height='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'm finally past the midpoint of this series. And I can't be more excited! <br/><br/>This time around I enjoyed Mat's POV best. From the character I most wanted to strangle he has become one of my favourites. I was warned that it would happen but he was so unbelievably stupid, selfish and annoying for most of the books so far that I couldn't see that happening. But he has grown a lot and is now someone that I not only like but also respect. And feel a bit sorry for. There was a situation when he was <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view</a></span>
  <span id="freeText16171360289451236736" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464420679i/19236518.jpg" width="350" height="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm finally past the midpoint of this series. And I can't be more excited! <br><br>This time around I enjoyed Mat's POV best. From the character I most wanted to strangle he has become one of my favourites. I was warned that it would happen but he was so unbelievably stupid, selfish and annoying for most of the books so far that I couldn't see that happening. But he has grown a lot and is now someone that I not only like but also respect. And feel a bit sorry for. There was a situation when he was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ raped by the Queen Tylin.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I understand that this was not what RJ intended and that it was supposed to be a lesson and a turning point for Mat but that doesn't change the fact that it happened against his will. Repeatedly. And when some of his companions learned they just laughed at him and told him that it's what he deserves. That he has finally had a taste of his own medicine. But at no point in the series has he been shown to force his attentions on someone. When a girl showed she's not interested he would simply transfer his attentions elsewhere. So there's a difference. I know I might come off as too sensitive but this is how rape culture is perpetuated. In fact there a second such thing in this book. And it happened to Queen Morgase. At least there RJ didn't try to show it off as something else but one of the Queens companions told her that she's acting weak afterwards. I would have been more worried if she wasn't affected. It's one of the greatest violations that can be done to a person and it's not something you can just forget or pretend it didn't happen. <br><br>But enough of that. There are three major plotlines here: one follows Rand's preparations for a showdown with Sammael and his dealing with the events that led to the battle at Dumai's Well, the second one is the hunt for the Bowl of Winds and the third one follows Egwene's attempts to whip the rebel Aes Sedai into a proper replacement for the White Tower and convince them to declare war on Elaida. <br><br>Rand was doing pretty well during this instalment. I loved how he brought the captured Aes Sedai down a few pegs. Some protest that he was too harsh but after all the attempts to manipulate him and trap him the Aes Sedai deserve a much harsher fate. In fact the Aes Sedai as a whole are among the groups I hate most in this world along with the Children of the Light and the Seanchan. All their machinations are only making things worse when they should be helping Rand wholeheartedly. But they're too used to being the ones in power and now the taste of being the ones who have to obey and follow is way too bitter for most of them. As a result they keep pushing and alienating the Dragon Reborn. It would serve them right if Rand wipes out the White Tower. I would love to see Elaida's face then. Min is a great influence on Rand and now that he has finally admitted his feelings for all three women (even if it's only to Min) I think he'll be able to move forward and stop seeing himself as a monster. Min is a calming force for him and that talent of hers is quite useful. Unfortunately Rand is still a bit reckless and so he gets himself in the dumbest and most dangerous situations. That new Aes Sedai that showed up - Cadsuane - is either going to be a great ally and adviser (once she stops pushing at him) or one who causes great trouble for him. I'm leaning towards the former but the jury is still out on this one. <br><br>At Ebou Dar Elayne and Nyneave are trying to find the Bowl of Winds so they can reverse the weather back to normal. That's all good and important but I can't help but being annoyed at Elayne. She's so irresponsible! I get that the weather thing is important but so are her people in Andor. There are other Aes Sedai that can be trusted to handle the Bowl but there's only one Daughter Heir. So she should have been back at Camelyn and taking care of her people. Instead she's playing Aes Sedai and then bitches about the way Rand is handling Andor. And every time someone tells her that Rand is waiting for her so he can give her the Lion Throne she trows a fit. What she doesn't seem to get is that he's not going to hang it to her as if it's a gift from him but rather as if he was a guardian of Andor for a while. And if she bothers to go to him and communicate she would know that. But no she prefers to sulk and ignore her responsibilities. Stupid spoiled girl. Nynaeve is still acting like a bitch and I want to slap her more often than not but she's showing signs of reverting to the awesome Nyneave from the beginning of the series. Now that Lan is with her I have high hopes. *fingers crossed* The way these two have treated Mat so far was despicable but Aviendha opened up their eyes about it. Or at least Elayne. Who would think that the Aiel savage is going to teach manners to the refined wetlanders :) From the women Aviendha and Birgitte are the only two that show sense and I loved them. I hope they won't become obstinate mules like the rest of the female cast. <br><br>Egwene is playing a very dangerous game. She did manage to establish her authority to some extend over the Rebel Aes Sedai. The joke's on them for thinking that they have chosen a figurehead but there's a Forsaken on the loose in their midst and some Black Ajah sisters. So Egwene needs to keep on guard. Instead she trusts people I would have had banished. For all they have learned over the last few months the Two Rivers gang is still way too trusting and naive. <br><br>Perrin is still having marital problems thanks to Beralaine's fixation on him. I sure hope that Faile will stop blaming him and turn her wrath on the real culprit. A catfight between those two will be hilarious! <br><br>Overall this book didn't move the plot forward much but it was still very interesting and exciting. </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="16171360289451236736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_280641911" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/280641911" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/280641911?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=on-deck">on-deck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2018">2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer280641911" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6838722146753444013">Of course there will be spoilers for the previous books, just a heads up for ya there.<br/><br/>This marks the halfway point in the Wheel of Time. I've finally made it ... halfway. It's no mean feat, so I'll take what I can get. This review may seem like a huge nitpick, and that would be right, so I don't know why I used the term "seem," but having said that, I really do love this series and I think I'm learning to enjoy the journey and the world instead of plot progression. It's really an amazing world t</span>
  <span id="freeText6838722146753444013" style="display:none">Of course there will be spoilers for the previous books, just a heads up for ya there.<br /><br />This marks the halfway point in the Wheel of Time. I've finally made it ... halfway. It's no mean feat, so I'll take what I can get. This review may seem like a huge nitpick, and that would be right, so I don't know why I used the term "seem," but having said that, I really do love this series and I think I'm learning to enjoy the journey and the world instead of plot progression. It's really an amazing world that I love being immersed in, so I have to keep reminding myself that the journey is what I bought the ticket for.<br /><br />Having said that (I feel like I've been saying this a lot lately), there are plenty of things to comment on and have fun with despite my immense enjoyment.<br /><br />I was warned about this book and the immense slow down that this series takes and it's not too surprising given the last couple books in the series, but it is still a bit frustrating (but see above!). The whole "bowl of winds" or whatever that's supposed to help the weather just seems like a total time waste. Have them go after forsaken, move forward armageddon, isn't that the reason for the crazy weather? I feel like I'm taking crazy pills. <br /><br />By my very accurate calculations, I'm pretty sure A Crown of Swords takes place in all of about 10 days. TEN DAYS is what 856 pages (mmpb) takes us! Are you kidding me! (please correct me if I'm wrong, I've been trying to google this important question)<br /><br />The next needs a bit of a stronger spoiler warning: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I'm a bit frustrated that Sammael's "death" wasn't a sure thing, which tells me it's not a sure thing, which makes the whole thing pretty much useless... which frustrates me more.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And what's with the cover of this book, that's quite the spoiler...<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[since Rand is passed out on his deathbed and Shadar Logoth still hasn't happened so you know it has yet to happen, that seemed like a bad idea on the cover.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />As frustrated as I was with a couple things in this, I have to say that Jordon completely had me on multiple occasions. First, with Perrin, and second with Rand. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rand's injury by Padan Fain, dang! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Overall, I really am learning to enjoy this series while it goes. I think rereading The Dragon Reborn (book 3) helped me in this process, even though I've had to remind myself over and again. TDR had about 10 pages of Rand so the slow down was already forcing its way in the story.<br /><br />4 out of 5 Stars (Might be my least favorite WOT book, but still high quality WOT stuff I've come to expect)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6838722146753444013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HKR2rDd2oS2PsqMv5vTmcOKF0gs6qJ15PsqUHVbP6WfdKll0GVq+aav+MQN0ZJ46Ky/6Zvk3w6ZQiDKNiYy2Ng==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GlWm1wC2l0P965XOFDB7rSA730UhK2UhsaM6x1l6xivb24kPLpqIB9mnB+KGoAPn6ZH3KOK0O/7f4ZxXhjmZeg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6767585736039191564"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br/><br/>Robert Jordan was the pen name of James Oliver Rigney, Jr., under which he was best known as the author of the bestselling The Wheel of Time fantasy series. He also wrote under the names <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/108933.Reagan_O_Neal' rel='nofollow noopener'>Reagan O'Neal</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/943931.Jackson_O_Reilly' title='Jackson O'Reilly' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jackson O'Reilly</a>.<br/><br/>Jordan was born in Charleston, South Carolina. He served two tours in Vietnam (from 1968 to</span>
  <span id="freeText6767585736039191564" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br /><br />Robert Jordan was the pen name of James Oliver Rigney, Jr., under which he was best known as the author of the bestselling The Wheel of Time fantasy series. He also wrote under the names <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/108933.Reagan_O_Neal" rel="nofollow noopener">Reagan O'Neal</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/943931.Jackson_O_Reilly" title="Jackson O'Reilly" rel="nofollow noopener">Jackson O'Reilly</a>.<br /><br />Jordan was born in Charleston, South Carolina. He served two tours in Vietnam (from 1968 to 1970) with the United States Army as a helicopter gunner. He was awarded the Distinguished Flying Cross with bronze oak leaf cluster, the Bronze Star with "V" and bronze oak leaf cluster, and two Vietnamese Gallantry Crosses with palm. After returning from Vietnam he attended The Citadel where he received an undergraduate degree in physics. After graduating he was employed by the United States Navy as a nuclear engineer. He began writing in 1977. He was a history buff and enjoyed hunting, fishing, sailing, poker, chess, pool, and pipe collecting. <br /><br />He described himself as a "High Church" Episcopalian and received communion more than once a week. He lived with his wife Harriet McDougal, who works as a book editor (currently with Tor Books; she was also Jordan's editor) in a house built in 1797. <br /><br />Responding to queries on the similarity of some of the concepts in his Wheel of Time books with Freemasonry concepts, Jordan admitted that he was a Freemason. However, "like his father and grandfather," he preferred not to advertise, possibly because of the negative propaganda against Freemasonry. In his own words, "no man in this country should feel in danger because of his beliefs."<br /><br />On March 23, 2006, Jordan disclosed in a statement that he had been diagnosed with cardiac amyloidosis, and that with treatment, his median life expectancy was four years, though he said he intended to beat the statistics. He later posted on his Dragonmount blog to encourage his fans not to worry about him and that he intended to have a long and fully creative life.<br /><br />He began chemotherapy treatment at Mayo Clinic in Rochester, Minnesota, in early April 2006. Jordan was enrolled in a study using the drug Revlimid just approved for multiple myeloma but not yet tested on primary amyloidosis.<br /><br />Jordan died at approximately 2:45 p.m. EDT on September 16, 2007, and a funeral service was held for him on Wednesday, September 19, 2007. Jordan was cremated and his ashes buried in the churchyard of St. James Church in Goose Creek, outside Charleston. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6767585736039191564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
